Mongolian Premier's Speech in Russia Receives Widespread Attention 23

Moscow. Moscow newspapers reported that Genden, the Premier of the "Mongolian People's Republic," spoke to reporters from various Moscow newspapers. Genden replied to reporters' inquiries, stating: "The actions of the Japanese and Manchukuo armies on the border of the Mongolian People's Republic last year have sufficiently demonstrated their aggressive nature and intentions. The Mongolian people have created their free and independent lives at a great price, with sacrifice and hard struggle. It has been fourteen years since then. We are engaged in peaceful construction, dedicated to developing the national economy, and improving the people's cultural standards and material lives."

"Before the establishment of the puppet Manchukuo, we had no border conflicts and enjoyed an independent and peaceful life. However, since the arrival of the Japanese army in Manchuria, the situation has drastically changed. The 'Manchukuo army' has attacked our borders, plundering the land of the Mongolian People's Republic. We have repeatedly sought a peaceful life and have repeatedly tried to reach a peaceful agreement, but all have failed."

Genden continued that the purpose of Japanese aggression is first to make the Mongolian People's Republic lose its independence and become a second "Manchukuo" in order to continue to attack China and the Soviet Union. "We do not want to succumb, but wish to protect our borders and independence. We can predict that when the Mongolian Republic is attacked by the Japanese and Manchukuo armies, it will cause an even greater reaction from other countries."

Genden also spoke about the Mongolian delegation's impressions of coming to Moscow, saying, "We maintain close and friendly relations with the great Soviet Union, and we constantly receive the warmest care and assistance. Every Mongolian herdsman knows that the Soviet Union is our friend. They deeply desire that Mongolia can develop peacefully, and they know that when we are victims of aggressors, they will surely come to our aid. I have come to Moscow to resolve some everyday problems."

Finally, Genden described the attack on the Manchukuo-Mongolian border by the Japanese and Manchukuo armies on December 19th last year, saying, "We have heard that they are preparing to launch another attack. We have warned 'Manchukuo' that if such attacks are made again, the serious consequences that will result will be borne by Japan and Manchukuo. We will certainly protect our independence and will not allow ourselves to be attacked. We have this ability and determination."

Genden also said that he believed that once Mongolia is attacked, it will receive the sympathy and assistance of countries that advocate peace. (TASS dispatch from the 4th)

Moscow. Genden, the "Prime Minister" of Outer Mongolia, and Demid, the "Minister of the Army," and their party have come to Soviet Russia for consultations. Foreign sources say that this trip is to conclude a secret military agreement with Soviet Russia. The official side of this question specifically denied it. As for the reason why the Outer Mongolian authorities are staying in Russian territory, the spokesperson of the People's Commissariat for Foreign Affairs refused to give any explanation. It is generally believed that the talks currently being conducted by the Russian and Mongolian authorities, with the participation of the Outer Mongolian "Army Minister" Demid, must be of a political nature. Foreigners believe that the Soviet Union's foreign policy has always emphasized pacifism, and that it is unwilling to clearly express that the interests of the Soviet Union and Outer Mongolia are the same, so as not to conflict with Japan. This decision by the Russian and Mongolian authorities to conduct talks, and to discuss in detail from a technical perspective the issue of Soviet national defense on the border with China, seems credible. (Havas dispatch from the 1st)

New Trends in the World Silver Problem: U.S. Treasury Secretary Negotiates with Mexican Treasury Secretary, and There is Talk of Holding an International Conference 24

Washington. Treasury Secretary Morgenthau stated today that negotiations between the U.S. authorities and Mexican Treasury officials are bound to benefit silver-using countries, and that close cooperation on this matter is truly beneficial to silver-producing countries. The decision to consult now is based on the procedure established by President Roosevelt when the Silver Purchase Act was passed. At that time, President Roosevelt said that the U.S. President intended to initiate talks on monetary policy with neighboring countries. Now Mexico is the first to come here for discussion. After this, the U.S. government will conduct similar discussions with other countries. Some people are asking whether Peru and Canada will be invited to discuss the matter. Morgenthau replied that it will be done separately, but that he cannot say much at this time. Senator Pittman, a silver advocate, said that Morgenthau has faithfully implemented the silver purchase procedures and that the method of silver talks is also commendable. Senator Thomas said that it is doubtful whether the Treasury Department is earnestly purchasing silver, and also said that the U.S.-Mexico talks may be a prelude to a world conference. The United States should first unite Mexico, Canada, and the silver-producing countries of South America, and then unite the silver-using countries of the Far East, in order to fight against managed currency groups. As for the events discussed in Washington, official circles in Mexico City are currently not commenting, but according to financial experts, silver price agreements must be under discussion. (Reuters dispatch from the 2nd)

Washington. Well-informed observers here stated yesterday that the recent confirmation that the United States has exchanged gold for silver from China may be intended to cooperate with Britain to consolidate China's currency plan. Treasury officials do not want to criticize this matter, but at the same time, some quarters cite China's December report on silver shipments to the United States to confirm this statement, and claim that the Treasury Department feels uneasy about the increase in U.S. gold reserves to over $10,000,000,000, considering this to be an unhealthy phenomenon. Senator Pittman's statement that gold will eventually flow out of the country to assist the stability of most countries makes this theory more forceful. The United States silently wishes for the strength of the Chinese government, because this kind of strength is a condition for cooperation in this ideal. (National Telegraph dispatch from the 3rd)

Washington. Treasury Secretary Morgenthau stated that his preliminary talks with Mexican Treasury official Suárez lasted an hour and were quite beneficial. They will continue to be held this week. Neither Morgenthau nor Suárez is willing to discuss the contents of the meeting with others. It is said that in addition to agreeing on a more detailed method for the U.S. Treasury Department to purchase Mexican silver, the talks between the two sides will also involve Mexico's implementation of a bimetallic reserve system. (Reuters dispatch from the 31st)

Washington. Treasury Secretary Morgenthau hinted today that the United States has already convened an international conference to encourage the adoption of gold and silver as currency standards based on an adjusted basis. At the same time, Morgenthau continued to meet with Mexican Treasury Secretary Suárez and said that satisfactory results have been achieved and that talks will continue on Monday. Regarding the question of whether silver-producing countries will unite to oppose the British pound and managed currency groups as advocated by Senator Thomas, Morgenthau said, "I believe that close cooperation is the duty of silver-producing countries." Morgenthau did not want to elaborate on this statement, but specifically asked the questioner to refer to President Roosevelt's message to Congress on the silver issue in 1934. In that message, President Roosevelt stated that the world's supply of silver is very large and its uses are very complex, so if the world wants to adopt gold and silver as the standard of prices, then the cooperation of silver-producing countries is essential. The President further stated, "We should seek a world agreement, but the United States may take action alone for its own interests. For this reason, I have consulted with several neighboring countries on the issue of adopting gold and silver as currency standards based on an adjusted basis. This agreement can often make the purchasing power of currency more stable than any standard to date." It is generally believed that Morgenthau's emphasis on President Roosevelt's statement proves that talks with other governments have entered an active and important stage. (National Telegraph dispatch from the 2nd)

Washington. Senate silver advocate leader Thomas said today that he hopes that the talks between the U.S. and Mexican financial authorities will ultimately lead to an agreement to convene a silver conference, with Mexico, the United States, and Canada participating. This conference will be the preliminary step towards a world silver agreement to fight against the trend of managed currencies. Thomas has repeatedly declared that if the silver purchase plan does not take effect, he will also implement managed currency in the United States as a self-defense measure. He further stated today that the entire silver issue is related to the forces of managed currency. If silver-producing countries cannot unite and use gold and silver as currency standards, they cannot compete with this kind of force even for a day. He hopes that Mexico, Canada, and the United States can agree on a bimetallic standard, and that Chile, Peru, and other Latin American countries can also participate later. Finally, it can be expanded to silver-using countries such as China and Egypt. The United States can exchange part of its gold reserves for silver, so that silver-using countries can also have an appropriate bimetallic reserve. (National Telegraph dispatch from the 1st)

Price Reduction for Tianjin-Pukou Railway Passenger Tickets 26

The second-class fare will be doubled, and the first-class fare will be doubled again. (Central News Agency dispatch from the 4th)

Ministry of Industry Sets Time Limit for Handling Public Petitions 27

Nanjing. The Ministry of Industry has formulated nine articles of rules for handling public petitions within a specified time limit, which were announced and implemented on the 4th. In addition to stipulating that the most urgent cases should be completed on the same day, and urgent cases should not exceed three days, cases such as applications for registration should be completed within five days. If the case requires a response or review from various departments, offices, divisions, or committees, the extension can only be a maximum of fifteen days. (Central News Agency dispatch from the 4th)

Nanjing. Since Article 5, Paragraph 1, of the Reflection Institute Regulations has special provisions, it should be handled in accordance with those regulations and should not be directly granted parole. (Central News Agency dispatch from the 4th)

Ministry of Finance Formulates Regulations for Inspecting Legal Tender 35

Nanjing. The Ministry of Finance has formulated nine articles of regulations for inspecting legal tender. This inspection report will be submitted to the Ministry of Finance for record each month, and the committee will announce a resolution to the people. (Special dispatch from the 4th)

Popular Science Talk

Discussing Red Leaves 56

— Editor-in-Chief of the Science Society of China, Zhang Chubao

People who live in cities are usually suffocated by the foul, turbid air, and feel very uncomfortable. But when they step onto verdant grass and admire green branches and leaves, they can't help but exhale deeply, feeling refreshed and filled with a sense of novelty. Green is the color that most easily stimulates human senses and brings pleasure. Trees present an inviting green color in their appearance, and physiologically, because their leaves contain chlorophyll, they can absorb the carbon dioxide exhaled by people and release the oxygen necessary for human respiration. Therefore, people who frequently spend time in forests are generally healthier than others.

As the seasons progress from late spring to mid-spring, and then to early and mid-summer, the leaves also gradually deepen in color from yellowish-green to light green to dark green. Day by day, the green deepens until autumn arrives. The pitiful green leaves, unable to withstand the pressure of the autumn wind, gradually lose their former luster and take on a dull color. The green slowly fades, and yellow or red takes its place. This is a melancholic time for trees. Just as the saying goes, "An old woman's yellowed pearls are worthless," trees at this time also evoke a similar sentiment. However, when we look into the mountains and forests at this time, the red light shines brightly, illuminating the entire mountain like a raging fire, and people experience another kind of interest. "Going to see the red leaves" becomes a seasonal activity in autumn. We will not imitate literary figures in composing poems or writing prose to appreciate red leaves. Instead, let us discuss the various aspects of red leaves from a scientific perspective.

First, let us ask: how are red leaves formed? The formation of red leaves is due to the presence of anthocyanins in the cells of the leaves. Anthocyanins are often found in the flowers, leaves, stems, and roots of plants, giving them a red, blue, or purple color, and often masking the green color of chlorophyll contained in the leaves, purely displaying these colors. Anthocyanins and chlorophyll are both pigments contained in cells, and they often coexist. Both are soluble in water, alcohol, or ether. According to Livingston and Maximov, when such a solution changes from acidic to neutral or alkaline, the color will also change from red to purple or blue, indicating that the color change is related to the change in acidity. According to Harvey, anthocyanins are related to glucosides (glucose derivatives present in plants, decomposed into glucose, alcohol, or other compounds by the action of alkali, acid, or enzymes) and have the same function: the formation of anthocyanins depends on the presence of glucose. Usually, whenever the environment is suitable for the production of a relatively high concentration of glucose in cells, such as at low temperatures or upon exposure to light, the occurrence of anthocyanins is more abundant. This may explain why red leaves are more commonly seen in the colder seasons of early spring and autumn.

Now that we know the cause of the formation of red leaves, we should ask: what is the significance of red leaves? What role do they play when leaves turn red? We know that there are two types of red leaves: normal red leaves and variant red leaves. Begonias and *Tradescantia zebrina* have red undersides of their leaves. Poinsettias (*Euphorbia pulcherrima*), and *Alternanthera ficoidea* have all or part of the leaves near the flower parts turning red. These all belong to normal red leaves, but their purposes are different. It is generally accepted by scholars that the red leaves of *Alternanthera ficoidea* and poinsettias indicate the location of the flowers to insects, facilitating pollination; but it is said that this is not the case for begonias and *Tradescantia zebrina*. It is generally believed that red color on the surface of leaves can be said to be a defense against excessively strong sunlight, reducing evaporation, but the red color inside the leaves is not the same. Many plants in the forests of Java are red early in the season. The air in the forest is very humid, so saying that it prevents sunlight and evaporation is naturally inappropriate. Therefore, Stahl explained that this is to absorb more of the red rays with high heat to increase evaporation, which is exactly the opposite of the previous explanation. The transformed red leaves are the red leaves seen in spring and autumn that I am going to discuss now. (To be continued)

Grand New Year Celebrations in Various Countries: Soviet Union Celebrates for the First Time Since the Revolution; Hitler Declares Last Year the Year of Freedom 57

Moscow: For the first time since the revolution, a formal New Year celebration was held today. Schools, factories, hostels, and theaters competed with each other in celebrations to demonstrate the reality of Stalin's recent declaration that "life is getting better." Thousands of people gathered in the city throughout the day to buy Christmas trees, which were strictly prohibited in the past. The Moscow Central Park held a skating competition, accompanied by military music, with more than 25,000 participants. Many entertainment venues were open all day. According to managers, sales of strong alcohol decreased, while sales of light alcohol increased, so there were fewer drunk people than in previous years. (1st, Reuters)

Moscow: The entire Soviet people joyfully celebrated the New Year. All newspapers published the great achievements of the Soviet Union last year. The *Pravda* editorial stated that the greatest achievement of the First Five-Year Plan was the elimination of unemployment in cities and poverty in rural areas, and that last year rapidly improved the lives of workers and peasants. The Soviet Union will not only be the richest country in the world, but also the most culturally developed country. Raising the cultural and technical level of the working class to be equal to that of engineers and technicians is the current task. Last year's economic success was enormous, with all sectors of the national economy completing their plans ahead of schedule. Transportation in various regions has been rapidly improved, and agriculture has completed its planned targets. The most important event was the widespread development of the Stakhanovite movement. This makes the historical struggle between socialism and capitalism certain to be won by the Soviet Union. As the Soviet Union enters the New Year, it can certainly guarantee even greater victories in the future. (3rd, TASS)

Tokyo: Prime Minister Okada released a New Year's statement, which briefly stated that our country has encountered various difficulties in the past few years, and now the country is in a state of leaping forward, which is also an inevitable situation. Under the Emperor's authority, we are very pleased to overcome these difficulties with the united strength of the people. However, the difficulties have not yet been resolved. The international conference on naval disarmament is currently being held in London, and the Japanese plenipotentiary representatives are working diligently to uphold just claims. Furthermore, there are still many domestic problems to be solved. At the beginning of this year, we sincerely hope that 100 million compatriots will cooperate and strive together to promote the development of the nation's fortunes. (1st, Domei News Agency)

Berlin: Head of State Hitler's New Year's address to the nation was broadcasted by Propaganda Minister Goebbels. He said, "The goal of this year is to maintain discipline, protect European culture, and fight against the enemy of mankind, namely, Bolshevism. Bolshevism aims to incite revolution and bloody tragedies to endanger world order and provoke various nations to be hostile to each other. This was the case in the past, and it will continue to be the case in the future." The Head of State then mentioned the rebuilding of armaments, saying that "Last year was the year Germany regained its freedom. After the revival of our country's army, our strength has increased even more, and therefore our responsibilities have become even greater. Recently, disturbances have occurred frequently in foreign countries, and comparing them with our country's clear and stable politics, the superiority or inferiority is self-evident." (1st, Havas)

Berlin: Hitler issued a New Year's address to the army, which said, "Germany has restored the freedom to arm itself and has re-established itself among the strong countries. I now express my gratitude to all officers and soldiers and to those who have contributed to the reorganization of the army. I am very pleased with the achievements of the past year, and I propose the slogan for 1936: 'March forward for peace, honor, and national strength!'" The German Army Chief also issued a New Year's address to the army, which briefly stated, "Since the reintroduction of conscription, the new year for serving the country and nation has now begun. We should unite and fight for Germany and the leader." This is sufficient to demonstrate the political concept of the German nation, but the unemployment problem has not yet been fully resolved, low wages have not yet been sufficiently raised, and the material and intellectual wealth of the entire country has not yet been able to provide opportunities for all the people to enjoy. "We need raw materials to overcome various difficulties, and these difficulties may not decrease in the coming year, but we have done our best to fight for this." (1st, Guomin News Agency)

New York: The New Year celebrations here today were the most lively since the New Year of 1928-29. Mayor La Guardia canceled the noise ban, so thousands of people gathered in Times Square with trumpets, sirens, and other noisemakers, playing music and blowing horns, creating a cacophony of sounds. At that time, the four characters "1936" made of electric lights atop a certain height shone brightly. The business of restaurants and taverns was the most prosperous in many years. Although the price of each ticket was five to ten dollars higher than last year, there was still no room for latecomers. A total of 1,100 licensed bars in New York were allowed to open all night, compared to 700 last year. More than 1,200 police officers were on duty in Times Square. (1st, Reuters)

Athens: Former Prime Minister Venizelos, who was originally the leader of the Republican Party, fled abroad after the failure of the revolution in March last year. He recently entrusted former Foreign Minister Roufas to send New Year's greetings to King George II, saying, "At the beginning of a new year, I wish that the constitutional monarchy of our country will be consolidated under the rule of Your Majesty, and that those who have been frequently involved in internal strife for 20 years can unite as one in the future." (3rd, Havas)

British Airline Airship Crashes in the Mediterranean Sea; Twelve Die 58

London: On Tuesday night, the Imperial Airways airship *Cathay* sank into the Mediterranean Sea while flying from Crete to Alexandria, killing twelve people, including two women. The only survivor was the pilot, Mr. Wilson, who was rescued by a British destroyer after floating in the water for six hours. He is currently hospitalized in critical condition. According to reports from Alexandria, the airship was carrying nine passengers, whose names are unknown, and four crew members, namely the pilot, Mr. Wilson, an engineer, a wireless operator, and a handyman. The airship had sent a wireless message stating that it had arrived in Alexandria, but unexpectedly sank into the sea a few miles from the mooring point in the port. British destroyers and tugboats rushed to the scene of the accident, but could not find the wreckage of the airship. The British destroyer *Glowworm* was the first to arrive and rescued Mr. Wilson. Although a thorough search was conducted overnight, no trace of the others was found. At dawn, aircraft joined the search, and two bodies were found yesterday afternoon, along with fragments of the crashed airship. The cause of the accident cannot be known until the pilot, Mr. Wilson, can speak and experts have examined the wreckage. It is believed that the three engines in the airship failed one after another within a few minutes. The sunken airship is currently being salvaged and may be salvaged within 24 hours. (2nd, Reuters)

U.S. Congress Opens; Roosevelt's Message Warns Warlike Nations; Advocates Using Moral Force to Resolve Wars; Economic Recovery is Effective, No Need to Increase Taxes 59

Washington: President Roosevelt delivered his annual message to Congress tonight, providing a comprehensive comparison of the world situation in early 1933 and the present.

The President recounted his inaugural address on March 4, 1933, to the joint session of the two houses, stating that the crisis at that time was purely national in nature. The ideal world was a peaceful illusion, and it was rationally hoped that obstacles to mutual trust and trade would be removed. Since then, the Good Neighbor policy has spread throughout the Western Hemisphere. As for the other parts of the world, the infighting is lamentable. Since the summer of 1933, the policies of the rulers of most major countries in Europe and Asia have not shown the path that peace and human goodwill should follow. As a result, the American people have had to acknowledge the growth of animosity, the trend of aggression, the competition of armaments, and the breakdown of emotions. The various factors at that time were sufficient to cause the tragedy of a general war. Most countries, if they could allow it to develop, would be willing to resolve their problems peacefully, but their rulers must consider the attacks of other rulers who cannot abide by the principles of improving the human race by peaceful means. The people of these countries blindly follow leaders who hope for autocratic power, hoping to expand their territory, correct the illegality of past wars, or seek outlets for selling goods and accommodating people. Because the people are impatient, they turn to believe in a policy of force or have the delusion that only they can accomplish a special mission. I admit that what I said is not something any country wants to hear. Their feelings can be obtained by those who hope for peace, but do not have to adopt scheming tactics, and the sympathy of the country. This is the common problem of diplomatic relations in Europe and Asia today. Ninety percent of the world's people are willing to abide by the current borders and reduce armaments. The remaining ten percent force other nations to arm themselves and restrict the continued efforts of the navy, so there is little success. The reason is sitting here. The policy of the United States hopes to limit armaments by peaceful means, resolve disputes by moral force, and oppose the high-pressure policies of autocratic classes.

The President cited the U.S. Neutrality Act, stating that if war cannot be avoided, then the countries of South and North America should maintain good order and neutrality, have sufficient national defense strength, and should do their best to mediate and restore peace to the belligerent countries. History proves that autocracy threatens peace, and countries that uphold democracy have never had such a crisis.

A small number of powerful financial and industrial organizations oppose the New Deal, but the government's reform plan has finally been completed. However, the representatives of the privileged class hope to regain political power. They borrow the constitution of the country to benefit themselves. It is no different from the fallacy of entrusting guardians and shareholders to use the property entrusted to them for political struggles.

The President also accused his political enemies of oppressing workers, shareholders, and consumers, and of proposing to abolish government programs, because they were confident that these proposals would hinder the recovery. The President continued to criticize enemies who openly advocate employing child labor, suppressing wages, abolishing social security procedures, terminating agricultural relief and work relief, and canceling the right of workers to organize. Do we really want to abolish the laws protecting investment and allow the people to be preyed upon by fraudulent speculators? The autocratic classes do not hope to restore the old system, but wish to seize centralized power. If we retreat step by step, then they will demand endlessly and will seize power and enslave the people. The autocratic classes intend to use the idea of terror to achieve their wishes.

The President cited the progress of industry and commerce, stating that the near balance of the federal budget is due to increased tax revenue, but the government has not levied new taxes. He is confident that there is no need to levy new taxes. The recovery has made significant progress, so the country's relief expenditure will be reduced in the future. The President asked Congress to move forward, saying, "I believe you will not disappoint the people in the future, because you have now faithfully met the expectations of the people." The President's speech was broadcasted across the country by wireless, and it is estimated that more than 15 million households listened to it. (3rd, Guomin News Agency)

U.S. House Proposes Permanent Neutrality Act; Expands the President's Power of Disposition 60

Washington: The Second Joint Session of the 74th Congress was held today. It is predicted that although the session will be short, the debate will be very fierce. The Chairmen of the Foreign Affairs Committees of the Senate and House, Pittman and McReynolds, jointly proposed the Neutrality Act after the meeting. The bill stipulates: Mandatory prohibition of the transportation of military materials to belligerent countries; Permission to prohibit the export of excess commodities, food, medicine, and major products; Mandatory prohibition of the trading of securities of belligerent countries, except for securities issued by non-governmental charitable organizations; Embargoes shall be implemented as soon as a state of war exists, but Congress may declare its opposition; The President may issue a statement that Americans who trade with the people of belligerent countries must bear the risk themselves. McReynolds further stated when proposing the bill that he intends to amend the bill so that countries in North and South America that are engaged in foreign wars are not bound by the bill, in order to comply with the spirit of the Monroe Doctrine. The two houses gradually agreed to listen to President Roosevelt's annual message tonight and then adjourned the meeting, reopening at 9:00 PM. At the same time, fifty members of Congress who support the Patman Bonus Bill held a meeting and decided to demand that the House consider the bill before January 13, at which time the bill will automatically be placed on the House agenda. Patman said that the committee intends to draft a joint plan at the meeting to be adopted by the Senate and House. We should end the issuance of tax-exempt securities, because our country has huge gold reserves and can issue good currency. (3rd, Guomin News Agency)

Washington: House Foreign Affairs Committee Chairman McReynolds introduced the permanent Neutrality Act in the House today, allowing the President to selectively prohibit the export of war materials and retain the existing power of prohibition. According to McReynolds, the authorities are satisfied with this bill. It was drafted only after lengthy consultations with President Roosevelt and State Department officials. Under this bill, the President may have the power to restrict the shipment of goods related to war, so that the amount shipped to belligerent countries is limited to the normal amount. However, food and medicine are not subject to this restriction. He will propose an amendment stating that if an American country is at war with a non-American country, then this American country may be exempt from the arms embargo. This bill prohibits financial dealings with belligerent countries. The purpose of this bill is to create a legal system to implement President Roosevelt's policy that any trade with belligerent countries is the responsibility of the merchants themselves and has nothing to do with the government. Senator Pittman also introduced a neutrality bill in the Senate this afternoon, allowing the President to restrict the amount of goods shipped to belligerent countries that exceeds the normal amount. Democratic Congressman Ludlow also introduced a third and more aggressive neutrality bill in the House, advocating that after the outbreak of war, the United States should prohibit the export of goods or any loans to belligerent countries. (3rd, Reuters)

Washington: The wartime Neutrality Act passed by Congress at the end of August last year, and promulgated by the President, will be effective until the end of February of this year. Now that Congress has reconvened today, House Foreign Affairs Committee Chairman McReynolds is about to introduce a new Neutrality Act to the House, intending to amend the current law to make it a permanent Neutrality Act. Its content advocates authorizing the President to act as he sees fit and expand the list of embargoed items. All raw materials necessary for war may be prohibited from being transported to belligerent countries without distinction, unless specifically authorized by the United States Congress. McReynolds recently announced that this bill had been discussed at length with President Roosevelt, and the government had deemed it appropriate. As for when Latin American countries are at war with countries outside the Americas, this provision cannot be used in general. An amendment is now being proposed to maintain the Monroe Doctrine and prevent aggression by countries outside the Americas. (3rd, Havas)

New York: The first reaction of the financial community here to President Roosevelt's address to Congress was that there were several reassuring points in the Head of State's speech, especially the fact that no new legislation was proposed. This shows that the time for respite is expected to be extended. The statement in the article that there is no need to levy new taxes is also welcomed by the public. President Roosevelt said that according to the current law, he believes that there is no need to levy new taxes or increase existing taxes. The recovery is now making great progress, so the country's relief expenditures can be reduced in the future. The Senate and House have now decided to extend the meeting until Monday of next week (3rd, Reuters)

Geneva: League of Nations officials and diplomats listened to the U.S. President's address to Congress via wireless before 4:00 AM this morning and paid close attention to it, because their words may have a significant impact on the League of Nations' future sanctions against Italy. In theory, how the League of Nations' sanctions are implemented has nothing to do with the United States, but in fact, those who maintain the League of Nations deeply hope that President Roosevelt will teach them. Current public opinion here believes that if President Roosevelt's remarks on belligerent countries are adopted by Congress, then the League of Nations' vote on the oil embargo against Italy can be taken one step further, because the United States has already set a precedent, and although the amount of oil that the United States normally exports to Italy can be kept as usual and not prohibited, the amount is not large enough to meet Italy's needs. (4th, Reuters)

London: Although the official circles here had high expectations for President Roosevelt's message to Congress yesterday, they are unwilling to express their opinions, and they are also unwilling to comment on the attitude taken by the United States towards belligerent countries. Those who actively advocate sanctions against Italy believe that President Roosevelt has issued a clear warning to aggressive and autocratic countries, but they especially dislike the fact that the Neutrality Act still has shortcomings. Some parties have expressed their joy, because many European countries have already expressed their opposition to the oil embargo against Italy, and now that the President of the United States has made a statement, it must be very persuasive. In short, those who enthusiastically advocated sanctions have now been greatly disappointed. (4th, Havas)

Rome: Official circles refused to comment on President Roosevelt's speech to Congress yesterday. Political observers believe that the oil embargo, although embarrassing to Italy in spirit, is not important economically, because Italy's reserves of liquid fuel are sufficient for the East African war. (4th, Havas)

Berlin: Diplomatic circles do not have a good impression of President Roosevelt's speech to Congress yesterday, fearing that after the United States adopts new measures on neutrality and expands the list of embargoed items, Germany will be forced to join the sanctions front against Italy and take actions that it is unwilling to take and are more severe in accordance with the outline set by the League of Nations. Up until now, every time Britain has tried to urge Germany to participate in sanctions, Germany has always said that other non-member countries, especially the United States, have not yet participated. Now that the position taken by the United States is similar to the League of Nations' policy, it will be difficult for Germany to refuse. As for the evolution of the neutrality issue in the United States, diplomatic circles here are paying sympathetic attention to it, and say that if the United States had refused to sell war supplies to belligerent countries in 1915, it would not have been caught up in the whirlpool of the European war. In some respects, it is believed that if the United States prohibits the transportation of oil to belligerent countries in accordance with the Neutrality Act, then the oil-producing countries in Europe will only be the three countries of Soviet Russia, Romania, and Britain, and they will naturally sit back and enjoy the benefits. In addition, political leaders have also greatly criticized President Roosevelt's remarks in his speech criticizing autocratic politics, saying that British Prime Minister Baldwin had previously criticized dictatorship in the same tone, which shows that Britain and the United States have formed a joint relationship and formed a joint front to oppose militarist dictatorship. This is almost a warning to Germany and its leader Hitler. (4th, Havas)

Anglo-Egyptian Relations Negotiations: Both Parties are in Initial Contact 61

Cairo: After Nahas, leader of the National Party, on behalf of the "National Front" composed of various political parties, expressed to Sir Lampson, the British High Commissioner in Egypt, his willingness to accept the Anglo-Egyptian Agreement of 1930, the new British Foreign Secretary Eden replied yesterday, saying, "I am urgently dealing with the Italo-Ethiopian dispute and have not yet been able to discuss the Egyptian issue at length. After Egypt holds elections and establishes a constitutional government, negotiations can naturally proceed without any objections." After receiving this reply, Egyptian Prime Minister Nessim told our reporter that Foreign Secretary Eden was not using delaying tactics. The British High Commissioner in Egypt, Sir Lampson, is scheduled to meet with Sidky, the leader of the Egyptian People's Party, tonight for discussions. Afterwards, representatives of various political parties in the "National Front" will gather at Prime Minister Nessim's official residence, and Sidky will report on the results of the meeting. (1st Havas dispatch)

London: Since the National Front, composed of various Egyptian political parties, issued a statement expressing its willingness to accept the Anglo-Egyptian Agreement of 1930, Britain and Egypt should immediately proceed with negotiations. The British Cabinet has decided to hold a meeting next Wednesday, and the Egyptian issue will be one of the important items on the agenda. The main points of the Anglo-Egyptian Agreement of 1930 are as follows: Egypt may join the League of Nations; neither of the contracting countries may conclude an alliance treaty with a third country that would harm the interests of the other party; the contracting countries shall conclude an alliance treaty to jointly resist foreign aggression; Egypt shall provide the British army with supplies and facilities for passage; the Suez Canal is of great importance, and Britain has the right to station troops at certain strategic locations in Egypt to protect it; the existing consular jurisdiction in Egypt shall be abolished; Sudan shall continue to be jointly administered by Britain and Egypt. The Egyptian National Party had previously expressed objections to the fourth and especially the sixth articles. Among them, Britain considers the following two items indispensable: (A) Britain must continue to station troops in the Suez Canal region and even in other locations in Egypt, especially given the Italo-Ethiopian dispute and the concentration of Italian troops in the Libyan colony; (B) Sudan should continue to be ruled by Britain, and Britain may allow the Egyptian government to participate in administrative matters there. In addition, Britain will insist on retaining British military advisors employed by the Egyptian army. As for the Egyptian police, which have been under British control, Egypt is eager to break free from these constraints, and Britain may accept a compromise, namely, the head of the police department may be an Egyptian, but the police advisor must be a Briton. Given this situation, there are already many difficulties in the negotiations between Britain and Egypt. It is generally believed that before starting negotiations, Britain will require the Egyptian government to stop anti-British demonstrations. (3rd Havas)

Cairo: The British High Commissioner in Egypt, Sir Lampson, met with Mamo, the leader of the Liberal Constitutional Party, last night to discuss British Foreign Secretary Eden's reply regarding the restoration of the Anglo-Egyptian Agreement of 1930. It is reported that Mamo still felt that Eden's reply had many loopholes and hoped that the British government would reconsider its answer. The "National Front," formed by a coalition of parties, insisted on accepting the draft Anglo-Egyptian Agreement negotiated by National Party leader Nahas and the late British Foreign Secretary Henderson in 1930. (3rd Havas dispatch)

Soviet Union's Foreign Trade Last Year 62

Moscow: The Soviet General Taxation Administration announced that the total value of the Soviet Union's foreign trade from January to October 1935 was 496,779,000 rubles, with exports of 299,112,000 rubles and imports of 197,667,000 rubles. Among the exported goods, light and heavy industry, timber, and food industry products accounted for 80.6%, while agricultural products accounted for only 18.3%. The trade during this period compared with the same period in 1934 is shown in the following table: (Ten months of 1934) (Thousands of Rubles) (Ten months of 1935) (Thousands of Rubles)

Exports: 343,022 299,112

Imports: 189,808 197,667

Total: 532,830 496,779

Trade Surplus: 153,214 101,445

From the above table, the export value in 1935 decreased slightly compared with 1934, while the import value remained largely unchanged. The decrease in exports was 43,910,000 rubles, mainly due to a decrease in food exports. At the same time, the export of heavy industrial products such as pig iron, machinery, and cement increased. For example, the export value of pig iron from January to October 1934 was 433,000 rubles, which increased to 2,814,000 rubles in 1935. The export of machine tools and electrical components increased from 2,520,000 rubles to 4,085,000 rubles. The export value of timber industry products was 75,305,000 rubles.

The Soviet Union's trade volume with various countries is as follows (Thousands of Rubles):

The Soviet Union's trade with various countries has changed slightly this year. For example, although the total export value has decreased, exports to Britain have increased by 9 million rubles compared with the same period in 1934, exports to the United States have increased by 10 million rubles, and exports to Iran have increased by more than 4 million rubles. Trade with Germany has decreased significantly, while French imports from the Soviet Union have increased significantly. (December 11th TASS communication)

Italian Planes Bomb Swedish Relief Team in Abyssinia: All of Europe Shocked; Dozens of Red Cross Personnel Killed or Wounded; Sweden Deems it a National Tragedy and Flies Flags at Half-Mast 63

London: According to a dispatch from the Abyssinian capital today, the Red Cross relief team recently sent to Abyssinia by Sweden was destroyed during an attack by ten Italian planes. All of Europe was shocked by this news. The number of deaths and injuries is still unknown, but according to the latest news, in addition to team leader Dr. Hylander and two other doctors, Smith and Holm, and one male nurse being injured, all other staff members died tragically. Dr. Hylander was injured in the back. The team was formed through national fundraising in Sweden. Upon hearing this tragic news, Sweden was filled with grief and anger, and many flew flags at half-mast to express their condolences. A certain newspaper in the Swedish capital stated that this news dealt a major blow to the country. The Italians' actions were a crime against international law. Italian planes actually dropped bombs on the relief team, which proves the brutality of the Italian army's combat methods. In the eyes of people all over the world, this behavior can be judged as Mussolini's barbaric war. The Abyssinian Emperor has sent a telegram of condolences to Prince Carl of Sweden. At the same time, a representative of the Abyssinian Red Cross has gone to General Desta's headquarters to investigate the matter. (1st Reuters dispatch)

Swedish Capital: The whole country now views the bombing of the Swedish Red Cross relief team by Italian planes as a national disaster. The International Red Cross has sent a telegram of condolences and stated that the Abyssinian representative, Dr. Junod, is now flying to the site of the disaster to conduct an investigation. Telegrams of condolences from all over the world are arriving in succession, including one from the British Red Cross. Several newspapers commented on this bombing as similar to the German submarine sinking the American ship Lusitania on that day. (2nd Reuters dispatch)

Swedish Capital: After yesterday's report of the Italian planes bombing the Swedish Red Cross relief team in Abyssinia, the Swedish people mixed shouts of "Revenge Italy" and "Down with Mussolini" with New Year's greetings. The Italian embassy here has been surrounded by mounted police dispatched by the authorities for strict protection. Last night, many "vigil gatherings" were changed to memorial services for the victims of the Red Cross team. Various organizations are now planning a large demonstration to protest the atrocities of the Italian planes. The exact number of deaths and injuries in the Red Cross team is unknown, but according to the latest news, in addition to team leader Dr. Hylander and two other doctors and one male nurse, all team members died tragically. (2nd Reuters dispatch)

Abyssinian Capital: According to the authorities, Italian planes bombed the Swedish Red Cross relief team and injured the team leader, Dr. Hylander. This is the second Swede injured. In addition, 30 Abyssinian wounded soldiers, 50 Abyssinian male nurses, and several soldiers were killed. According to reports received here, a total of 12 Italian planes flew over the area where General Desta's troops were stationed and dropped leaflets signed by General Graziani, stating that Abyssinian troops had brutally murdered an Italian air force officer, so they must be retaliated against. Fifteen minutes later, Italian planes dropped many heavy bombs from an altitude of several thousand feet, including gas bombs. Among the dead were two Italian wounded soldiers who were being operated on by doctors. (2nd Reuters dispatch)

Abyssinian Capital: When Italian military planes bombed the city of Dolo on the southern route, the Swedish Red Cross rescue team was affected. Team leader Dr. Hilander and his Abyssinian assistant Langsterro were seriously injured at the time. Dr. Hilander arrived in the capital this morning and told our reporter that his assistant had died of his injuries. (4th Havas dispatch)

Geneva: The Abyssinian government sent a strongly worded note to the League of Nations because Italian military planes bombed the Swedish Red Cross rescue team. According to the latest news, the Abyssinian government threatened that if Italy continued to act in violation of international law, it would confiscate Italian property in Abyssinia as retaliation. (3rd Reuters dispatch)

Swedish Capital: The people, angered by the Italian planes bombing the Swedish Red Cross rescue team in Abyssinia, are now urging the Red Cross not only to send a team to replace the previous team, but also to send hundreds of doctors and nurses to Abyssinia to show revenge. Many young people across the country are enlisting. It is now expected that the team destroyed by Italian planes will soon be replaced by a new team. Today, according to a public announcement, although the latest news is not as serious as the initial reports, the perpetrators have not been able to reduce their guilt. According to Roman semi-official documents, the Italian air force took this retaliatory action because it heard that an air force lieutenant was captured by Abyssinian troops and then brutally murdered. During the attack, a document was dropped saying, "You will get your due revenge." The document also stated that the bombs of the Italian planes fell into the Swedish Red Cross camp, seemingly injuring two Swedes. In this battle, many Abyssinian soldiers were killed or injured. The Abyssinian government issued a statement declaring that the Italian authorities' claim to cover up their atrocities, that Abyssinian troops had murdered an Italian air force officer, was a despicable lie. At the same time, the International Red Cross has asked the Italian military authorities to order Italian planes not to attack two Abyssinian planes carrying two wounded Swedish doctors to General Desta's headquarters. (3rd Reuters dispatch)

Abyssinian Capital: The government has just issued a bulletin, describing the situation on Monday when Italian military planes bombed the Swedish Red Cross rescue team in Dolo City, on the front line of the southern route of Wogadun. The bulletin stated, "At 7:00 a.m. that day, twelve Italian planes flew to the defense area of Prince Desta on the southern route and dropped leaflets signed by General Graziani, the commander-in-chief of the Italian southern route. The content stated that two Italian air force personnel had been beheaded and displayed by Abyssinian troops, and the Italian army had to retaliate. Fifteen minutes later, these Italian planes flew to the location of the Swedish rescue team and dropped bombs from a height of several hundred meters, several of which contained poison gas." (2nd Havas dispatch)

Swedish Capital: A special dispatch from our correspondent regarding the bombing of the Swedish Red Cross rescue team in Dolo City, Abyssinia, by Italian military planes, announced here that there were no Swedish casualties. After this news came out, people's hearts were greatly relieved, but various evening newspapers still greatly criticized the Italian air force's atrocities. The "Arlunda" newspaper expressed hope that Sweden would be stimulated to endorse the League of Nations' sanctions policy against Italy. According to Italian military planes, before dropping bombs, they flew very low, and they must have been able to see the Red Cross signs and the Swedish personnel in the service group at a glance. The executive committee of the Swedish Red Cross attaches particular importance to this. (4th Havas dispatch)

London: Sweden originally had no diplomatic representative stationed in the capital of Abyssinia. After the Swedish Red Cross rescue team in Dolo City, Abyssinia, was bombed by Italian military planes, the Swedish government asked the British government to investigate the incident on its behalf. The Foreign Office has instructed Sir Barton, the British Minister to Abyssinia, to conduct an investigation. As for the protection of the lives and property of Swedish overseas Chinese in Abyssinia, Sir Barton has also been instructed to do so. (2nd Havas dispatch)

Swedish Capital: Regarding the case of the Italian military planes bombing the Swedish Red Cross rescue team in Dolo City, Abyssinia, although there were no Swedish casualties, powerful sources here still believe that the issue of the Italian military violating international Red Cross conventions has not been resolved. As for the handling of this case, there will be no action until the report from Sir Barton, the British Minister to Abyssinia, and the Red Cross has not yet been sent. However, the newspapers are urging the Italian government to lodge a protest and demand that the responsible personnel be punished and compensate for the losses. According to Italian military planes, before dropping bombs, they flew very low, and they must have been able to see the Red Cross signs and the Swedish personnel in the service group at a glance. The executive committee of the Swedish Red Cross attaches particular importance to this. (4th Havas dispatch)

Abyssinian Capital: Dr. Hylander, the leader of the Swedish Red Cross rescue team, met with Reuters correspondent Mr. Collins today and described the situation of the Italian military planes destroying the team near Dolo. Dr. Hylander angrily said, "This was a completely deliberate action. In the days before the bombing, Italian military planes often fired machine guns around the team. On the morning of the bombing, I was working in the operating room when suddenly bombs and machine gun bullets rained down. I just saw two rows of Italian military planes, three in each row, attacking the rescue team, and I was already hit by bullets and lost consciousness. When I opened my eyes again, I saw a tragic scene in front of me that was heartbreaking. Dozens of people were lying dead or wounded around me. Those who were injured but not dead were either screaming in pain or groaning. The tents were on fire and burning fiercely, which increased the panic. I cannot estimate how many bombs the Italian military planes dropped, at least over two hundred, and tens of thousands of machine gun bullets. After inspection, there was one tent with 425 bullet holes. The total number can be imagined. Deputy Medical Officer Longstrem, although seriously injured, still shouted, 'I must save the wounded!' Another assistant, Longgren, was slightly injured and immediately rescued the wounded. The Swedish and Abyssinian male nurses who escaped serious injuries worked very bravely, but the tents were on fire, the smell of bombs was irritating, and the crowd was in panic, so the work was very difficult. All the medicines we had prepared were destroyed by the bombs, so today we can only use very crude methods to treat the wounded. After the bad news spread, the soldiers under General Desta rushed to clear the debris and hide the wounded in a safe place, fearing that the Italian military planes would return. The Italian military's actions cannot be excused under any circumstances, because our team abides by international conventions and hangs the Red Cross sign high, which can be seen by Italian military planes in the sky. The Italian military's claim that Abyssinian leaders and soldiers were hiding in the Red Cross rescue team is absolutely unfounded. Even the guards provided by General Desta do not live with the rescue team. My assistants outside the operating room at the time of the bombing said that the Italian military planes were flying very low." Dr. Hylander, after being injured that day, flew from the southern route front to the Abyssinian capital by plane, accompanied by another Swedish doctor, Mr. Smith, three Abyssinian people, and the team's mascot, an antelope. The antelope was also injured during the bombing by the Italian military planes. The plane carrying Dr. Hylander and others was a Fokker giant plane, driven by Baron Rosen, and arrived here from the southern route front through an unknown wasteland. Only one foreign journalist, Mr. Collins, was at the airfield. When the plane landed and the engine stopped, the moans and cries of pain of the wounded could still be heard in the sound of the propellers rotating. The first person to appear from the plane was Dr. Hylander, who staggered into the waiting ambulance, followed by three seriously injured Abyssinian people, Dr. Smith, and an antelope. (4th Reuters dispatch)

Italy and Abyssinia Prepare for a Major War 64

London: The general headquarters of the Italian and Abyssinian armies are now busy preparing for a large-scale offensive. The most intense battles since the start of the war three months ago are about to break out. The location of the major battle seems to be on the northern front. Italian planes have been unusually active on the southern front recently. The Abyssinian army now views this as a precursor to the Italian army launching an attack from this section first. However, General Naiyabu, the commander-in-chief of the Abyssinian army on the southern route, has completed his preparations for an early offensive. Dagabur was bombed fiercely by four Italian planes again yesterday, but there were no reports of deaths or injuries. At the same time, according to news from the Abyssinian capital, the Italian army outposts on the northern front have retreated from the southeast, south, and southwest of Magale because Abyssinian General Mullugushtai is now leading the Abyssinian elite, including a portion of the Imperial Guard, attacking from the southeast and is unstoppable. It is reported that Mr. Mullugushtai has also received the assistance of 12,000 troops from Abyssinian Emperor's cousin, General Gemane. At the same time, the Abyssinian capital is now recruiting new soldiers. All able-bodied men who have not served in the military must report the reasons for not enlisting. Today, an edict of Abyssinian Emperor was read on a certain street in Harar, which said, "Anyone who intends to evade military service to defend against the enemy, I will personally punish them." The document ordered the people of the entire province who are able to wield a spear to register in Jijiga by the end of January. Deserters and those who evade enlistment will be severely punished. (3rd Reuters dispatch)

London: According to news from various sources, on New Year's Day, the Abyssinian war, in addition to the major battle in Danane on the Somali Front, the town of Danane, located on the western side of Kelagehai, which is strategically important in transportation, was captured by the Italian army after a courageous melee. In this battle, both sides used rifles, bayonets, and sharp blades to fight. According to Italian military planes, about 100 Abyssinian soldiers died and many were injured, while the Italian army suffered fewer casualties. (2nd Reuters dispatch)

It is reported that he will use planes and light tanks to assist in the battle. His troops have increased from 45,000 to 75,000. A total of 12,000 members of the Militia have been sent to East Africa, two-thirds of whom have arrived in Somalia. It is reported that there is another entire division, totaling 18,000 men, which will be transferred from Libya to Somalia. The first batch has already passed through the Suez Canal. Another division of Madama soldiers transferred from Italy to Libya will replace them. In the next few weeks, Somalia will begin to rain, and the Italian authorities are eager to achieve a major victory in February. It is now believed that General Graziani's first task will be to establish solid flank defenses to defend against the offensive of General Desta, the governor of Sidamo, who is related to the Abyssinian Emperor. However, the general attack will likely be launched at Sasabane. Major Barnes, Reuters war correspondent, recently went to the Dolo front. Thousands of soldiers are camped outside the town of Ruf Filandi, surrounded by transport vehicles equipped with machine guns. Both Italian and Ethiopian soldiers seem eager to fight. Northern Manchuria - Discovery of a Land of Little People - Men Under Three Feet Tall - Total Population Over 800 67

The Manchuria Daily News reported that on December 23 last year, the Harbin Railway Bureau's Railway Hospital, in order to investigate the sanitation along the railway lines under its jurisdiction, sent doctors to various locations along the lines to investigate the situation. Unexpectedly, a surprising "village of little people" was discovered near "Wuchang" and "Lade" on the Labin line. The village has a population of over 800 people, all of whom are under three feet tall, and they do not like to talk to ordinary people, forming a unique tribe of their own. Their lives are semi-primitive and they have no culture to speak of. Since the recent opening of the railway, modern culture has gradually been reflected in their minds, and they regard it as a terrifying thing, so they look at general society with disdain. The most incredible thing is that those with short stature are entirely men, while the women are relatively tall. Currently, Dr. Lizi Wang of the Railway Bureau's Mental Hospital has gone to the land of little people and selected 30 people to bring to Harbin to vigorously study their physiology. According to the hospital's doctors, the water quality in the area where the tribe lives is very poor and contains a large amount of iron. However, it is still questionable whether this is the cause of their stunted growth, as the tribe's daily food is the same as that of other Manchurians. However, due to their short stature, their operational efficiency is less than half that of ordinary people. Currently, anthropologists have obtained this rare data, which is causing a great sensation.

President Chiang's New Year's Day Broadcast Address - The Essential Path to National Self-Salvation and Saving the Nation - Laying the Foundation of National Morality and Spirit with the New Life Movement - Promoting the Progress of Material Civilization with the National Economic Construction Movement 76

President Chiang delivered a speech on New Year's Day at the Central Broadcasting Station, entitled "The Essential Path to National Self-Salvation and Saving the Nation." The original text is as follows: "Fellow countrymen across the country, today is the first day of the 25th year of the Republic of China. It is a day for all of us to rejoice and celebrate together. Although I cannot personally meet with you all at this time, I can speak to you personally on the radio, which is a very gratifying thing. I would like to take this opportunity to talk to all of you about the most important tasks for our country and all of our fellow countrymen this year. As everyone knows, the situation in our country is very dangerous and urgent, and we are in a state of crisis at every moment. However, the fate of the nation is entirely determined by all of us. If we want to save the Republic of China, which is shared by 400 million fellow countrymen, and if we want to revive the most ancient and glorious Chinese nation in history and culture, I believe that one thing lies in the efforts of the Republic of China itself. In other words, it lies in the efforts of 400 million fellow countrymen, that is, every citizen of the country must be able to work hard and be self-reliant. As the saying goes, 'The rise and fall of the world is the responsibility of every individual.' Now that everyone knows that the nation is in such a crisis, everyone, no matter who they are, should take these two maxims to encourage themselves, understand their duties, take responsibility, be of one heart and one mind, work together, have firm aspirations, unite in spirit, and advance bravely together towards the goal of saving the country and the people. We must understand that saving the country is not such a difficult thing. As long as everyone can make tireless efforts to do what they can do, I believe that no matter how urgent the crisis our country is in, we can save it within this year, so that it can turn from danger to safety, from weakness to strength, and from misfortune to blessing. We know that no matter which country, when it wants to be rebuilt, or which nation, when it wants to strive for revival, it must suffer many disasters and encounter great dangers. Conversely, a large country and a weak nation will never truly awaken and strive for self-improvement and revival if they do not encounter many disasters and great dangers. Therefore, although our country and nation are now suffering unprecedented disasters and encountering enormous dangers, we not only do not need to be pessimistic or worried, but we can also see that the more foreign disasters and the greater the current dangers, the faster the opportunity for the revival of our country and nation will come. The ancients said, 'A country that has no external enemies will perish.' They also said, 'Sorrow in the legs and feet is what inspires sages, and many difficulties are what revive a nation.' This is the meaning of this. Our Chinese nation has the most ancient and glorious history of 5,000 years, the beautiful rivers and mountains of 40 million square miles, and even more 400 million fellow countrymen who account for a quarter of the world's population. Look at which country or nation in the world can compare to our greatness? As long as all of our citizens can strengthen their confidence in the nation and truly stand on their own and be self-reliant, what else is there to fear or worry about? Our country can definitely be saved, our nation can definitely be revived, and it can be revived starting this year.

From now on, how should we be self-reliant and self-reliant? Or, what are the methods of saving the country and reviving the nation in the future? As I said just now, as long as everyone does what they can do well, it is self-reliance, and it is the way to save the country and revive the nation. The most important and most basic point is the New Life Movement, which everyone has known about and has been working hard to promote for the past two years. The meaning of the New Life Movement is to enable all of our fellow countrymen to restore the inherent moral spirit of our Chinese nation - propriety, righteousness, integrity, and honor - and to first realize it in daily life habits such as food, clothing, housing, and transportation, so that our citizens, each and every one of them, can at all times and in all places understand propriety, righteousness, integrity, and honor, and no longer do anything that is contrary to propriety and righteousness, lacking in integrity and honor, and use propriety, righteousness, integrity, and honor to establish the personality of ourselves and the entire nation, and wash away all the past shame of each of us and the entire nation. A person must have a noble and independent personality in order to be qualified as a modern citizen, to be worthy of being a modern citizen, and the country must also have a dignified and independent personality in order to be qualified as a modern country, to be worthy of being a modern country. Whether it is an individual or a country, as long as one's own real personality can be established, no one will dare to bully us, and no country will dare to invade our country. Otherwise, not only will people oppress us and invade us, but they will also destroy us. As the saying goes, "People must insult themselves before others will insult them, and a country must attack itself before others will attack it." This is a definite principle. Therefore, if you want people not to bully, oppress, or invade us, the only way is for everyone to encourage themselves and strive to establish the personality of modern citizens, which is to work together to establish the personality of our country, and the basic effort is to restore the inherent moral spirit of our nation. The inherent moral spirit of our nation is actually the basic requirement that the citizens of all civilized countries, ancient and modern, Chinese and foreign, must possess. Therefore, all of our fellow countrymen must keep in mind at all times the two sentences "understand propriety, righteousness, integrity, and honor" and put them into practice. All the previous chaotic, scattered, perfunctory, lazy, extravagant, lascivious, selfish, apathetic, numb and insensitive corrupt lifestyles must be swept away and eradicated. It is not good to continue to be confused and be a backward person of the barbaric era, but to resolve to "die yesterday and live today", remove the old and establish the new, and practice the "orderly, clean, simple, diligent, fast, and reliable" new life, and be a "understand propriety, righteousness, integrity, and honor" new citizen. Once we all become modern new citizens, we can certainly establish a modern, civilized, strong new country, and we can certainly stand shoulder to shoulder with others and stand on the basis of freedom and equality. (To be continued) International Commercial Telegraph
